## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Old Consumer API to New Consumer API Migration

## Your Task

Analyze the migration from the old Kafka consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the new KafkaConsumer API in apache/kafka. Find Java source files that (1) implement the legacy ConsumerConnector interface, (2) implement the new KafkaConsumer API, and identify the key behavioral differences in offset management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

## Kafka Repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489)

The legacy `kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector` interface was part of the old Scala-based Kafka consumer API (pre-0.9). This version of the Kafka repo appears to be a modern version (post-0.9) that has already removed the old Scala-based consumer API. The old ConsumerConnector is not present in this repo.

The new KafkaConsumer API files:
1. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java` - The main public-facing consumer class that implements `Consumer<K, V>`. It delegates to either `ClassicKafkaConsumer` or `AsyncKafkaConsumer` based on the group protocol configuration.
2. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java` - Implements `ConsumerDelegate<K, V>`, uses the classic group protocol (pre-KIP-848). This is the "old" implementation within the new API.
3. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java` - Implements `ConsumerDelegate<K, V>`, uses the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848). Network I/O happens in a dedicated background thread.
4. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java` - Interface that both ClassicKafkaConsumer and AsyncKafkaConsumer implement.
5. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java` - Factory that creates either ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer based on group.protocol config.
6. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java` - Manages coordination for the classic protocol, including auto-commit.

---

## Research Findings: Kafka Consumer API Migration

### Legacy ConsumerConnector Files
**None found in any of the three repos.** The old `kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector` (Scala-era, ZooKeeper-backed, pre-0.9 API) has been fully removed from these modern versions of Kafka, Flink, and Camel. The closest analog to "legacy" within the current codebase is `ClassicKafkaConsumer`, which the Kafka codebase itself labels as the "legacy group protocol" implementation.

---

### New KafkaConsumer API Files Found

#### `kafka--0753c489` (Apache Kafka)
| File | Role |
|------|------|
| `clients/.../consumer/KafkaConsumer.java` | Public facade; delegates to `ConsumerDelegate` |
| `clients/.../consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java` | Internal interface extending `Consumer<K,V>` |
| `clients/.../consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java` | Factory: picks `ClassicKafkaConsumer` vs `AsyncKafkaConsumer` based on `group.protocol` config |
| `clients/.../consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java` | Classic group protocol (pre-KIP-848); single-threaded I/O; uses `ConsumerCoordinator` for offsets |
| `clients/.../consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java` | New KIP-848 protocol; dedicated `ConsumerNetworkThread`; uses `CommitRequestManager` |
| `clients/.../consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java` | Offset coordinator for `ClassicKafkaConsumer` |
| `clients/.../consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java` | Offset commit manager for `AsyncKafkaConsumer` |
| `examples/.../kafka/examples/Consumer.java` | Usage example showing `poll()` loop, `commitSync()`, rebalance listener |

Let me summarize what I've found:\n\n## Kafka Repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489)\n\nThe legacy `kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector` interface was part of the old Scala-based Kafka consumer API (pre-0.9). This version of the Kafka repo appears to be a modern version (post-0.9) that has already removed the old Scala-based consumer API. The old ConsumerConnector is not present in this repo.\n\nThe new KafkaConsumer API files:\n1. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java` - The main public-facing consumer class that implements `Consumer<K, V>`. It delegates to either `ClassicKafkaConsumer` or `AsyncKafkaConsumer` based on the group protocol configuration.\n2. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java` - Implements `ConsumerDelegate<K, V>`, uses the classic group protocol (pre-KIP-848). This is the \"old\" implementation within the new API.\n3. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java` - Implements `ConsumerDelegate<K, V>`, uses the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848). Network I/O happens in a dedicated background thread.\n4. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java` - Interface that both ClassicKafkaConsumer and AsyncKafkaConsumer implement.\n5. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java` - Factory that creates either ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer based on group.protocol config.\n6. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java` - Manages coordination for the classic protocol, including auto-commit.\n7. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java` - Manages offset commits for the async (new) consumer.\n\n## Camel Repository (sg-evals/camel--1006f047)\n\nThe Camel Kafka component uses the new KafkaConsumer API:\n1. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java` - Camel's consumer that extends DefaultConsumer, manages KafkaFetchRecords threads.\n2. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaFetchRecords.java` - Runnable that uses `org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.Consumer` (the new API).\n3. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/DefaultKafkaClientFactory.java` - Creates `org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.KafkaConsumer` instances.\n4. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java` - Abstract base for commit managers.\n5. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/SyncCommitManager.java` - Synchronous offset commit.\n6. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AsyncCommitManager.java` - Asynchronous offset commit.\n7. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitToOffsetManager.java` - Commits to an offset repository.\n8. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitManagers.java` - Factory for commit managers.\n9. `components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/NoopCommitManager.java` - No-op commit manager (for auto-commit).\n\n## Flink Repository (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc)\n\nThe Flink repo doesn't have a Kafka connector in the main codebase (it's in a separate repo). The Python wrapper `flink-python/pyflink/datastream/connectors/kafka.py` has `FlinkKafkaConsumerBase` and `FlinkKafkaConsumer` classes.\n\n## Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\n\n### Old ConsumerConnector API (legacy, pre-0.9):\n- Offsets were committed automatically by the consumer framework (Zookeeper-based)\n- No explicit `commitSync()` or `commitAsync()` methods\n- Offsets stored in Zookeeper\n- Thread-based model with message streams\n\n### New KafkaConsumer API:\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (classic group protocol):\n  - Offsets stored in Kafka broker (not Zookeeper)\n  - Supports both auto-commit (via `enable.auto.commit=true`) and manual commit\n  - Manual commit via `commitSync()` (blocking) or `commitAsync()` (non-blocking with callback)\n  - Auto-commit happens periodically during `poll()` calls\n  - All network I/O in the calling thread\n  \n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (new consumer group protocol, KIP-848):\n  - Network I/O in a dedicated background thread (`ConsumerNetworkThread`)\n  - Offset commits managed by `CommitRequestManager`\n  - Uses `CompletableFuture` for async operations\n  - Implements new consumer group protocol with server-side assignment\n\nThe task asks specifically about:\n1. Files implementing the legacy ConsumerConnector interface\n2. Files implementing the new KafkaConsumer API\n3. ZooKeeper is no longer involved in offset management. This is true for both ClassicKafkaConsumer and AsyncKafkaConsumer.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"ConsumerCoordinator.java sends OffsetCommitRequest to the group coordinator broker. CommitRequestManager.java similarly sends OffsetCommitRequest via the ConsumerNetworkThread.\"\n      },\n      {\n        \"dimension\": \"Auto-commit mechanism\",\n        \"legacy_consumer_connector\": \"Auto-commit was handled by a background AutoCommitScheduler thread that periodically committed offsets to ZooKeeper independently of the application thread. The interval was controlled by auto.commit.interval.ms.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_classic\": \"Auto-commit is triggered lazily during poll() calls. ConsumerCoordinator.maybeAutoCommitOffsetsAsync() is called inside the poll() path; it checks a timer and fires commitOffsetsAsync() when the interval expires. There is no separate background thread \u2014 the application thread drives commits.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_async\": \"Auto-commit is scheduled by CommitRequestManager on the ConsumerNetworkThread. The application thread enqueues events; the background thread processes them. This decouples commit I/O from the application poll() call.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"ClassicKafkaConsumer.java line 612: coordinator.maybeAutoCommitOffsetsAsync(time.milliseconds()) called inside poll(). ConsumerCoordinator.java lines 1196-1202: maybeAutoCommitOffsetsAsync() checks timer expiry. CommitRequestManager.java implements RequestManager processed by ConsumerNetworkThread.\"\n      },\n      {\n        \"dimension\": \"Manual commit API\",\n        \"legacy_consumer_connector\": \"No explicit manual commit API. The ConsumerConnector.commitOffsets() method committed all offsets for all streams to ZooKeeper synchronously. There was no per-partition granularity or async variant.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api\": \"Explicit commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>) and commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, OffsetCommitCallback) with per-partition granularity. commitSync() blocks until the broker acknowledges. commitAsync() returns immediately; the callback is invoked on the next poll().\",\n        \"evidence\": \"ClassicKafkaConsumer.java lines 745-750: commitSync calls coordinator.commitOffsetsSync() with timeout. Lines 771-774: commitAsync calls coordinator.commitOffsetsAsync(). Camel SyncCommitManager.java line 75: consumer.commitSync(offsets, Duration.ofMillis(timeout)). Camel AsyncCommitManager.java line 73: consumer.commitAsync(offsets, callback).\"\n      },\n      {\n        \"dimension\": \"Commit on close behavior\",\n        \"legacy_consumer_connector\": \"Calling ConsumerConnector.shutdown() triggered a final synchronous commit to ZooKeeper before releasing resources.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_classic\": \"ConsumerCoordinator.maybeAutoCommitOffsetsSync() is called during close() with a timer. If auto-commit is enabled, it performs a final blocking commitSync. If the timer expires before completion, the commit is abandoned with a debug log.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_async\": \"AsyncKafkaConsumer enqueues a CommitOnCloseEvent to the ConsumerNetworkThread, which processes it before the thread shuts down. This ensures pending commits are flushed asynchronously before close completes.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"ConsumerCoordinator.java lines 1178-1188: maybeAutoCommitOffsetsSync() with WakeupException/InterruptException handling. AsyncKafkaConsumer.java imports CommitOnCloseEvent (line 48).\"\n      },\n      {\n        \"dimension\": \"Threading model for commits\",\n        \"legacy_consumer_connector\": \"A dedicated AutoCommitScheduler background thread performed commits independently. The application thread and commit thread were separate, which could cause race conditions.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_classic\": \"Single-threaded: all network I/O (fetching, committing, heartbeating) happens on the application thread during poll(). The consumer is explicitly NOT thread-safe. Commits are serialized with fetches.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_async\": \"Two-thread model: application thread enqueues ApplicationEvents (including AsyncCommitEvent, CommitEvent); ConsumerNetworkThread dequeues and processes them, sending actual OffsetCommitRequests to the broker. Results are returned via CompletableFuture or BackgroundEvents.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"AsyncKafkaConsumer.java imports ApplicationEventHandler, ConsumerNetworkThread, AsyncCommitEvent, CommitEvent. ClassicKafkaConsumer.java comment at line 79 of examples/Consumer.java: 'the consumer instance is NOT thread safe'.\"\n      },\n      {\n        \"dimension\": \"Error handling on commit failure\",\n        \"legacy_consumer_connector\": \"ZooKeeper commit failures were typically retried silently by the background thread. Application code had limited visibility into commit failures.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_classic\": \"commitSync() throws CommitFailedException or RetriableCommitFailedException on failure. commitAsync() delivers the exception to the OffsetCommitCallback. ConsumerCoordinator tracks in-flight async commits (inFlightAsyncCommits AtomicInteger) and retries on retriable errors.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api_async\": \"CommitRequestManager handles StaleMemberEpochException (re-enqueues with updated epoch), RetriableException (retries), and non-retriable errors (completes the CompletableFuture exceptionally). The application receives failures via the future or callback.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"ConsumerCoordinator.java lines 1185-1188: catches WakeupException/InterruptException during auto-commit sync. No per-partition control.\",\n        \"new_kafka_consumer_api\": \"commitSync() and commitAsync() accept a Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, allowing per-partition offset commits with arbitrary metadata strings. The no-arg variants commit all current positions. Camel's SyncCommitManager and AsyncCommitManager commit one partition at a time using singletonMap.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"Camel SyncCommitManager.java lines 72-75: Collections.singletonMap(partition, new OffsetAndMetadata(lastOffset)). The commit() method is a NO-OP; only commit(partition) writes to the repository. This allows offset tracking to survive consumer restarts without relying on Kafka's __consumer_offsets topic.\",\n        \"evidence\": \"CommitToOffsetManager.java lines 36-53: commit(partition) calls saveStateToOffsetRepository(); commit() is NO-OP.
